## MANDATORY: Use Sourcegraph Code Search Tools BEFORE Any Code Changes

You have Sourcegraph MCP tools available (keyword_search, nls_search, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read). You MUST use them as your primary code discovery method.

Use `list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.

**CRITICAL — TWO-PHASE WORKFLOW:**

### Phase 1: Search & Understand (MANDATORY — DO NOT SKIP)
BEFORE writing ANY code, modifying ANY file, or running ANY implementation command, you MUST:
1. Read the task instructions and identify key functions, classes, files, or concepts mentioned
2. Make at least 3 Sourcegraph search calls to find and understand the relevant code:
   - Use `keyword_search` with the repo filter to find specific symbols/identifiers from the task
   - Use `list_files` to understand the project structure
   - Use `go_to_definition` / `find_references` to trace code relationships
3. DO NOT start implementing until you have searched for the key terms from the task
5. Use `deepsearch` for dependency/impact analysis — understand blast radius of changes, find callers of modified functions, downstream consumers of changed interfaces, and tests covering affected code paths
6. `deepsearch` returns a polling link, NOT immediate results. After calling it, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times — Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete
8. For code review tasks: the PR diff alone does NOT show full impact. Use `deepsearch` to find what else depends on the changed code before finalizing your review

### Phase 2: Implement
After understanding the codebase through Sourcegraph:
1. Use Read to verify local file contents (Sourcegraph indexes latest branch, local may differ)
2. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
3. Make your code changes — stop searching, focus on implementation

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide.

# [VS Code] Fix Stale TypeScript Diagnostics After Git Branch Switch

**Repository:** microsoft/vscode  
**Difficulty:** HARD  
**Category:** big_code_feature
**Task Type:** Feature Implementation - Large Codebase

**Reference:** [Trevor's Big Code Research](../../../docs/TREVOR_RESEARCH_DEC2025.md#1-vs-code-stale-diagnostics-after-git-branch-switch)

## Description

Users are seeing stale TypeScript diagnostics in the Problems panel after switching Git branches. Files that no longer have errors still show the old errors until the user manually opens each file and makes an edit. It seems like the diagnostics pipeline only refreshes on in-editor changes and misses file-on-disk changes from Git operations.

## Task

This task requires implementing code changes to fix stale diagnostics.

### Required Implementation

Check the full diagnostics flow from a text change through the extension host to the Problems view, identify where file system changes should trigger diagnostic updates, and propose where we'd need to add listeners to fix this.

### Implementation Steps

1. **Understand the diagnostics pipeline**:
   - Find the main diagnostics collection and how it stores errors per file
   - Locate the extension host communication for sending diagnostics to the client
   - Find the Problems view panel and how it subscribes to diagnostics
   - Look for existing file change listeners (e.g., `deleteAllDiagnosticsInFile`, `onWillChange`)

2. **Identify where diagnostics are currently refreshed**:
   - Find the text change event handlers that trigger re-diagnostics
   - Understand how the diagnostics pipeline reacts to document changes
   - Look for any existing file system watchers or listeners

3. **Add file system change triggers**:
   - Add listener for file changes on disk (e.g., from `git checkout`)
   - Trigger diagnostics refresh for changed files
   - Clear stale diagnostics for files that no longer exist
   - Re-run TypeScript/language server analysis for affected files

4. **Test the fix**:
   - Switch branches that change TypeScript errors
   - Verify stale diagnostics are cleared
   - Verify new errors are shown after branch switch
   - No duplicate diagnostics appear

5. **Verify no regressions**:
   - All tests pass: `npm test`
   - No performance regression from additional file watchers
   - Diagnostics still work for in-editor changes

## Success Criteria

[x] Stale diagnostics are cleared when files change on disk  
[x] New diagnostics appear after Git branch switch  
[x] Diagnostics refresh without requiring manual file edits  
[x] Problems panel reflects current state of files  
[x] All tests pass: `npm test`  
[x] No performance regression  
[x] Code follows VS Code conventions and patterns  

## Testing

```bash
npm test
```

    16→function diagnosticsEquals(a: vscode.Diagnostic, b: vscode.Diagnostic): boolean {
    17→	if (a === b) {
    18→		return true;
    19→	}
    20→
    21→	return a.code === b.code
    22→		&& a.message === b.message
    23→		&& a.severity === b.severity
    24→		&& a.source === b.source
    25→		&& a.range.isEqual(b.range)
    26→		&& arrays.equals(a.relatedInformation || arrays.empty, b.relatedInformation || arrays.empty, (a, b) => {
    27→			return a.message === b.message
    28→				&& a.location.range.isEqual(b.location.range)
    29→				&& a.location.uri.fsPath === b.location.uri.fsPath;
    30→		})
    31→		&& arrays.equals(a.tags || arrays.empty, b.tags || arrays.empty);
    32→}

   251→	public get capabilities() {
   252→		if (this._configuration.useSyntaxServer === SyntaxServerConfiguration.Always) {
   253→			return new ClientCapabilities(
   254→				ClientCapability.Syntax,

186-assistanttext-
Now I understand the pipeline well. Let me also look at `bufferSyncSupport.ts` line 513-530 where `listen()` is defined:

Looking at `bufferSyncSupport.ts:513-530`, the `listen()` method registers these event handlers:
1. `onDidOpenTextDocument` → opens text document in buffer
2. `onDidCloseTextDocument` → closes text document 
3. `onDidChangeTextDocument` → handles in-editor changes, triggers diagnostics
4. `onDidChangeVisibleTextEditors` → re-requests diagnostics for visible editors

The problem is clear: there is no handler for **file changes on disk** that happen outside the editor (e.g., from `git checkout`). When TypeScript files change on disk due to a branch switch:
1. The TS server is not notified about the file content changes
2. The old diagnostics remain in the `DiagnosticsManager`
3. The Problems panel shows stale errors

Let me check how VS Code handles file save events and what `onDidSaveTextDocument` does.

212-assistanttext-
While that compiles, let me now plan and implement the fix. Based on my analysis:

**Current Flow:**
1. `BufferSyncSupport.listen()` only listens to `onDidOpenTextDocument`, `onDidCloseTextDocument`, `onDidChangeTextDocument`, and `onDidChangeVisibleTextEditors`
2. When a git branch switch happens, files change on disk but VS Code doesn't fire `onDidChangeTextDocument` for files that aren't open in the editor
3. The TS server already has file system watchers (via `createFileSystemWatcher`) that tell it about file changes. However, these feed into the TS server's own project system, not directly into the diagnostics refresh pipeline
4. The `bufferSyncSupport` never re-requests diagnostics for synced buffers when their underlying files change on disk

**The Fix:**
I need to add a file system watcher in `BufferSyncSupport` that detects when files that are currently synced (open in editor tabs) change on disk, and re-requests diagnostics for those files. This mirrors how a git branch switch would change file contents.

218-assistanttext-
Now I have a thorough understanding. Let me implement the fix. The key issue is in `bufferSyncSupport.ts` - when files change on disk (e.g., from git checkout), the TS server's internal project system gets notified through file watchers, and it produces new diagnostics. However, the `BufferSyncSupport` doesn't actively request diagnostics re-evaluation for currently open/synced buffers when files change on disk.

The fix needs to happen in `BufferSyncSupport.listen()` where we should add a listener that watches for file changes on disk and triggers diagnostics refresh for synced buffers that changed.

221-assistanttext-
Now let me implement the fix. The approach:

1. In `BufferSyncSupport.listen()`, add a file system watcher for TypeScript/JavaScript files
2. When files change on disk, check if those files are in the synced buffers

After
	public listen(): void {
		if (this.listening) {
			return;
		}
		this.listening = true;
		vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(this.openTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(this.onDidCloseTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(this.onDidChangeTextDocument, this, this._disposables);
		vscode.window.onDidChangeVisibleTextEditors(e => {
			for (const { document } of e) {
				const syncedBuffer = this.syncedBuffers.get(document.uri);
				if (syncedBuffer) {
					this.requestDiagnostic(syncedBuffer);
				}
			}
		}, this, this._disposables);
		this.listenForDiskFileChanges();
		vscode.workspace.textDocuments.forEach(this.openTextDocument, this);
	}

	private listenForDiskFileChanges(): void {
		// Watch for file changes on disk (e.g., from git branch switches) to refresh
		// diagnostics for synced buffers whose underlying files may have changed.
		const fileWatcher = this._register(
			vscode.workspace.createFileSystemWatcher('**/{*.ts,*.tsx,*.js,*.jsx}')
		);

		const onDiskFileChange = (uri: vscode.Uri) => {
			if (!this.handles(uri)) {
				return;
			}
			// File changed on disk but may not have triggered an in-editor content change.
			// Request diagnostics refresh so stale errors are cleared.
			this.requestAllDiagnostics();
		};

		this._register(fileWatcher.onDidChange(onDiskFileChange));
		this._register(fileWatcher.onDidCreate(onDiskFileChange));
		this._register(fileWatcher.onDidDelete(uri => {
			if (!this.handles(uri)) {
				return;
			}
			this._onDelete.fire(uri);
			this.requestAllDiagnostics();
		}));
	}

const ts = require('typescript');
const path = require('path');
const fs = require('fs');

// Read and parse tsconfig
const configFile = ts.readConfigFile('src/tsconfig.json', ts.sys.readFile);
const parsedConfig = ts.parseJsonConfigFileContent(configFile.config, ts.sys, 'src');

parsedConfig.options.noEmit = false;
parsedConfig.options.outDir = path.resolve('out');
parsedConfig.options.declaration = false;
parsedConfig.options.sourceMap = false;

let count = 0;
for (const fileName of parsedConfig.fileNames) {
  const sourceText = fs.readFileSync(fileName, 'utf8');
  const result = ts.transpileModule(sourceText, {
    compilerOptions: parsedConfig.options,
    fileName: fileName,
  });
  
  // Calculate output path
  const relPath = path.relative(path.resolve('src'), fileName);
  const outPath = path.join(path.resolve('out'), relPath.replace(/\.ts$/, '.js'));
  const outDir = path.dirname(outPath);
  fs.mkdirSync(outDir, { recursive: true });
  fs.writeFileSync(outPath, result.outputText);
  count++;
  if (count % 500 === 0) process.stderr.write('Transpiled ' + count + ' files\n');
}
process.stderr.write('Done: ' + count + ' files transpiled\n');

const ts = require('typescript');
const path = require('path');
const fs = require('fs');

// Read and parse tsconfig
const configFile = ts.readConfigFile('src/tsconfig.json', ts.sys.readFile);
const parsedConfig = ts.parseJsonConfigFileContent(configFile.config, ts.sys, 'src');

parsedConfig.options.noEmit = false;
parsedConfig.options.outDir = path.resolve('out');
parsedConfig.options.declaration = false;
parsedConfig.options.sourceMap = false;
parsedConfig.options.isolatedModules = true;

let count = 0;
let errors = 0;
for (const fileName of parsedConfig.fileNames) {
  try {
    const sourceText = fs.readFileSync(fileName, 'utf8');
    const result = ts.transpileModule(sourceText, {
      compilerOptions: {
        ...parsedConfig.options,
        isolatedModules: true,
      },
      fileName: fileName,
    });
    
    // Calculate output path
    const relPath = path.relative(path.resolve('src'), fileName);
    const outPath = path.join(path.resolve('out'), relPath.replace(/\.tsx?$/, '.js'));
    const outDir = path.dirname(outPath);
    fs.mkdirSync(outDir, { recursive: true });
    fs.writeFileSync(outPath, result.outputText);
    count++;
    if (count % 500 === 0) process.stderr.write('Transpiled ' + count + ' files\n');
  } catch(e) {
    errors++;
    if (errors <= 3) process.stderr.write('Error transpiling ' + fileName + ': ' + e.message + '\n');
  }
}
process.stderr.write('Done: ' + count + ' files transpiled, ' + errors + ' errors\n');
" 2>&1

globalThis._VSCODE_PACKAGE_JSON = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync('package.json', 'utf8'));
globalThis._VSCODE_FILE_ROOT = 'file://' + path.resolve('out') + '/';

async function run() {
  const Mocha = (await import('mocha')).default;
  const mocha = new Mocha({ ui: 'tdd', timeout: 5000 });
  
  const testFiles = [
    'out/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/extHostDiagnostics.test.js',
    'out/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.js',
    'out/vs/platform/markers/test/common/markerService.test.js',
  ];
  
  for (const file of testFiles) {
    const fullPath = path.resolve(file);
    if (fs.existsSync(fullPath)) {
      mocha.addFile(fullPath);
    } else {
      console.log('File not found:', fullPath);
    }
  }
  
  mocha.run(failures => {
    process.exit(failures ? 1 : 0);
  });
}

  console.error(e);

const path = require('path');
const fs = require('fs');

// Setup globals
globalThis._VSCODE_PRODUCT_JSON = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync('product.json', 'utf8'));
globalThis._VSCODE_PACKAGE_JSON = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync('package.json', 'utf8'));
globalThis._VSCODE_FILE_ROOT = 'file://' + path.resolve('out') + '/';

async function run() {
  const Mocha = (await import('mocha')).default;
  const mocha = new Mocha({ ui: 'tdd', timeout: 5000 });
  
  const testFiles = [
    'out/vs/platform/markers/test/common/markerService.test.js',
  ];
  
  for (const file of testFiles) {
    const fullPath = path.resolve(file);
    if (fs.existsSync(fullPath)) {
      mocha.addFile(fullPath);
    } else {
      console.log('File not found:', fullPath);
    }
  }
  
  mocha.run(failures => {
    process.exit(failures ? 1 : 0);
  });
}

run().catch(e => {
  console.error(e);
  process.exit(1);
});

async function run() {
  const Mocha = (await import('mocha')).default;
  const mocha = new Mocha({ ui: 'tdd', timeout: 5000 });
  
  const testFiles = [
    'out/vs/platform/markers/test/common/markerService.test.js',
    'out/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/extHostDiagnostics.test.js',
    'out/vs/workbench/api/test/browser/mainThreadDiagnostics.test.js',
    'out/vs/workbench/contrib/markers/test/browser/markersModel.test.js',
  ];
  
  for (const file of testFiles) {

    if (fs.existsSync(fullPath)) {
      mocha.addFile(fullPath);
    } else {
      console.log('File not found:', fullPath);
    }
  }
  
  mocha.run(failures => {

  });
